Ragnarok is one of my favorite Marvel movies.  Love and Thunder seemed to try to repeat most of the Ragnarok tropes, but everything seemed . . . off.  Clumsy.  Over-the-top, but not in an effective way.  Most of the jokes were just off enough that they didn't land for me.  I felt like each scene was rushed in order to get to the next one, with weak connections between them.  There is so little explanation for Jane becoming Thor - just one flashback, a quick shot the hammer self-assembling, and BOOM, she is a fully-formed Thor kicking ass and that's that.  Are you kidding me?  I want to see that transformation!  Can we at least get a montage?  Jane and Thor seem to have very little chemistry.  Natalie Portman is a great actress but her attempts at humor just don't land for me (I think the writing was just off).  Ragnarok is great because Thor shows some vulnerability and humor, while still retaining some dignity and godlike presence.  In Love and Thunder, this is pushed to the point where he is an absolute bumbling moron.  There is nothing he doesn't screw up.  It's just . . . off.  The Zeus scene was a jumbled, frenetic mess.  I found Russel Crowe extremely annoying and his accent just seemed like something you'd find in a middle-school play.  Over the top and clumsy.  I feel like someone (maybe not Taika) went "just take what you did in Ragnarok and dial it up another notch", resulting an a chaotic, forced, disjointed mess.  Hey, we have a classic rock soundtrack - check.  Slow motion jumping shots - check.  Completely useless Guardians of the Galaxy cameo (where none of them seemed excited to be in the movie" - check.  I thought Christain Bale's opening scene was great, though.  Until he ran into the God who was clumsily, one-dimensionally bad for the sake of being bad so Gorr would be justified killing him.  Can't he have a tiny bit of nuance?  Can't Gorr feel some conflict in killing his god?  This movie just does not work, and I couldn't make it all the way through.  Perhaps this is evidence of just how much of an achievement Ragnarok was, where despite lots of silliness everything was perfectly calibrated.  It just WORKED.  Maybe it's just one of those things that can only be pulled off once.    All I know is that whatever magic made Ragnarok work was completely absent in Love and Thunder.

Chris, I gotta say man, I'm just not sure this "don't talk about what I dislike" thing is a little overboard. In fact, I get why you're doing it. It makes sense, y'know, cuz you have a movie being made and obviously it would suck to be criticized about something you've made when you've criticized films heavily in the past (yourself). I'm not saying your film will be bad... but criticism is still criticism at the end of the day. People (hopefully) learn from criticism, not get deterred from it. You'll always be a critic first in my eyes, filmmaker second. You don't have to hate on a film like maybe you've done in the past, but maybe more videos like this where you talk about what you liked about the movie (and maybe what you would've done a little differently yourself) would always be nice. I think what they're doing with Thor is interesting. No, this movie isn't as strong as many other MCU films, but there's at least a consistent theme going on with Thor lately. That theme, to me, is "What do you do when your life has been completely changed?" and it's something that I feel a whole lot these past several years.   Thor: Ragnarok was an exploration of Thor learning that his family's dark past was more problematic than he comprehended, his decision on whether or not he was going to obsess over that or if he was going to do what he could to help those in need.   Avengers: Infinity War saw Thor having to deal with a threat that was out of his element, while his losses were compounded from the previous movie. We got to see him adapt and plan, while also forging new bonds with the Guardians of the Galaxy.   Avengers: Endgame did something really interesting, not just with his character, but with all the MCU cast. The running theme of that movie seemed to be all about how the characters processed trauma and how they grieved. Some of them responded by trying to help others as much as possible, as Captain America did, and others were just so overcome with their sense of failure and loss. Thor was one of the latter, as shown with his weight gain and unhealthy behavior, along with an implication that he'd become an alcoholic.   This movie is continuing where Endgame left off with his character, that being that he's working to overcome his negative behaviors and grow from the trauma he's suffered. However, it's not just like flipping a switch. We learn that he doesn't have a great history with processing loss even before the Snap, and that cost him his relationship with Jane. He's still kind of adrift, and it takes another crisis to get him to focus and actually process his emotions.

Hated this movie .. sucked ass ...
From what I've heard from other reviews (particularly Jeremy Jahns' review), a trend that I've seen that leads to Thor 4 (while still enjoyable)  not clicking with people as much stem from _Thor: Love and Thunder_  having TOO much jokes, to the point where it detracts from the film? That was always a lingering issue I had with _Thor: Ragnarok_ , where I liked the humor but it's excessive focus on the humor clashed with the dramatic tone it was trying to convey the other half of the time. Often times, it felt like you were watching two different movies that were mashed together. You had the gravitas of Odin's death and Hela conquering Asgard be undercut by all the jokes that Thor would make that undercut that gravitas. I think that similar to that, in Thor 4, the issue seems to be rather than Thor simply making jokes, it feels like he becomes the joke? That it feels like people are laughing at him rather than with him? That if Taiki Watiti (an immensely talented director whose usually really great at balancing tones of comedy and drama, as shown in _Jojo Rabbit_ )  was really going to commit to the humorous tone, that they should have the antagonists and stakes match that rather than feel like Thor and the main antagonists are from 2 different movies?   Honestly, I think why I consider Guardians Vol 2 and the Ant-Man films to have the right balance while considering Thor: Ragnarok to be too jokey is because of scale, stakes, and expectations. The Ant-Man films have never had end-of-the-world stakes but instead more personal stakes that affect only a select few people close to the characters. The scale of the stakes in comparison  to the humor in the Ant-Man films felt appropiate. Meanwhile with Guardians Vol 2, while the scale is certainly much bigger, it's crux lied in the very grounded, human-like emotional journey of Peter Quill/Star-Lord. It helps that the GotG films never really took themselves that seriously.    Now contrast that with the latest 2 Thor films, where the scale and expectations are much bigger. The main characters in the Thor films aren't humans or humanoid aliens but gods or at least advanced aliens mistaken for gods. When your antagonists are Hela the Goddess of Death and Gorr the Butcher of Gods, there's a rather high expectation of scale and expectations. The expectations set by Hela and Gorr being such menacing cataclysmic foes that cleave through and threaten the people and civilization of Asgard comes with it a certain expectation of gravitas and seriousness. A civilization-ending threat necessitates some gravitas.  If instead the set expectation was more like Hela or Gorr had killed a group of Asgardian children or a personal friend of Thor's like one of the Warriors Three, and Thor had set out on a quest for revenge, then the constant humor and joking wouldn't clash with the tone nearly as much because the scale and expectations are set more appropiately. There would still be stakes and dramatic moments but the scale and set  expectations of the main antagonists and how much of a threat they menace to be is scaled appropriately to the tone and humor.    It's not like the MCU haven't been able to balance humor with drama, especially when it comes to Thor. If the humor and jokes were used as a defense/coping mechanism to help with fear and trauma, like we see with Thor in _Infinity War_ and _Endgame_ , then it'd be understandable and appropriate in a sense. But when the jokes are made just because and it goes from laughing with Thor making jokes to laughing at Thor as the joke, that's when the clashing of tones is really apparent.    Concurrently, we never really see Gorr actually butcher his way through gods. I feel like that was such a letdown. Gorr is supposed to be a serial killer of _gods_ . I would've liked some more Hannibal Lecter shit, ya know? Have him massacre a few gods and/or show off a wall of grisly trophies like the heads or signature weapons of a few gods from different pantheons. Something to actually show and justify to us why Gorr deserves the title Butcher of Gods.   Instead, Hela (or Thanos) has a better showcase as a Butcher of Gods than Gorr the God-Butcher does.   Do you get what I mean? Does that describe the sort of disconnect that some people justifiably  feel with Thor 4?

*To the people disappointed in the new direction this channel is taking:*  Let's get one thing out of the way: Yeah, I also found Stuckmann's channel more entertaining when he gave grades for movies and made his yearly best/worst-lists. I miss this stuff, but still I wouldnt call his new direction a disappointment or even a "sell-out".   Selling out would be, if Chris continued his old concept just to get more clicks, even if he doesn't like doing it anymore. What's happening right now, is the exact opposite. Like another commenter here already said, it's a transitional phase. Those phases are always a little murky and this is reflected by the content. The content still isn't fully adapted to the new direction and hasn't found it's groove yet. It's a in-between kinda thing. Which might make the content seem a little wishy-washy sometimes. Like there's still something missing.   But when it comes to Chris, I know he'll get there eventually. It's not the first transitional phase he went through, even if those earlier phases might have been not that obvious. So instead of using shallow phrases like "selling out", the more interesting question would be: *Why do you watch this channel?*  Is it because you are interested in Chris as a person? Or do you simply need another movie reviewer who is praising the movies you love and trashing the movies you hate? If it's the latter, you'll find a ton of those on youtube. Many of them doing the same stuff for over a decade now. But by your logic, delivering the same lame product over and over again, doesn't mean selling out. ;)  If you watch, because you are interested in Chris as a person, this transitional phase is a very interesting thing to witness. Yes, it might not be as entertaining as before. Yes, it might be a little bumpy and not every video feels as well rounded as the older stuff. But still, after following this channel for ca. 10 years now, for me it is really exciting to see Chris finally get to this point of his life. Because after watching him for so long, it was always very obvious how much he was longing to get there.   In his whole career as a movie reviewer there were always those little moments where you could feel he wanted to do something else. Even many years ago he already stated on several occasions that trashing movies isn't really that much fun for him. That he has so much respect for the movie making process and that it's getting harder for him to talk negatively about the creative endeavors of people who might have failed, but who still put tons of work and passion into the creation of the movie.   Chris began to realize how many things can go wrong during a movie production and that sometimes it's just that one decision that can destroy your whole work. A decision you might not have any influence on. A studio decision, a marketing decision, a budget decision... whatever. After realizing that Chris became more interested to find out how the whole production process works on a professional level and why it can go so incredibly wrong many times, but also can turn out so incredibly amazing many other times. This did interest him much more than simply saying "movie bad" or "movie good" and give grades that often were very one-sided and didn't fully reflect his whole opinion about the movie.   For me the answer to "Why do you watch this channel?" is pretty clear: I'm watching because I'm interested in Chris as a person. At first it might have been just the reviews, but over the span of all those many years, watching Stuckmann's personal journey (from movie nerd to movie critic to movie maker, while also becoming a husband and father inbetween) was what made me continue watching. It not only made me continue watching, it made me grow a much bigger personal attachment to this channel than most others. When Chris is releasing a new video, for me it's not just new content to waste some time and be entertained. No, it's more like a new page in a diary of a person I really like and appreciate.   So if your only reason for being here is to watch more of the same movie critic content that you can find plentiful on youtube, I somehow understand your disappointment. But if you're here for the person behind the content, this transitional phase is one of the most exciting periods this channel has ever gone through: finally witnessing how Chris Stuckmann is able to fulfill his lifelong dream.   Greetings from Germany :)

We like Thor and we like Valkyrie but what about the other Gods? We needed to see more of these other Gods. We needed to see the good they could do and why getting rid of some Gods is Bad.  And Gorr's plan was "steal a magic axe to open a magic door so he can meet a space genie who will give him a wish to destroy all gods". What? Why was the magic door asgardian? Why was Eternity locked up? Presumably Odin did this when he was bringing "order" to the universe with Hela but why? Is Eternity in the habit of just handing out wishes, so Odin sealed him away? We needed to _see_ this.  How did Gorr know Eternity will just grant people wishes if they go round his house for tea? Is this common knowledge? His plan was then attack New Asgard and kidnap the children to then lure Thor into the Shadowlands to steal his axe... It didn't seem like that was his plan at that time. It seemed made up on the fly. We needed to _see_ more of this.  Why was the rainbow bridge suddenly in stormbreaker or mjiolnir? The rainbow bridge was operated and controlled by Heimdal who could see through time and space.   I could go on. And maybe this is what Marvel is trying to step aside from: make a movie w/ personal stakes and not the apocalypse. From what I can tell, you not wanting to poke fun at bad movies is related to you realizing what it would be like to be at the receiving end of it. The thing is, no one will hold you to a higher standard than a fellow director or a movie critic. The effect and reaction depends on the author, not the critic. Compare the way Tommy Wisseau took all the criticism thrown his way with how M. Night Shyamalan took it. Tommy rolled with it, accepted it, "adopted the meme" and people both like and respect him for it. Shyamalan added whole scenes in his movies just to caricaturize movie critics, and it made him look pretty bad. If something in a film is silly, I think it's fair to point it out. Most film critics don't personally attack the authors, but their works, and that's okay.

I think Covid really changed the MCU. I think the level of importance people put into the stories, letting them brew for a little over a year before anything new came out, changed the momentum they had. It put a lot more importance into EndGame and made people forget how long it took to get there. Just look at the numbers New Rockstars was doing during the pandemic. They grew a ton even pre-Wandavision. That's all these people who were re-watching the movies and growing a deeper connection to the projects and a level of excitement that just wasn't the same pre-covid. We're not watching movies leading to Infinity War, we're basically back in the new Phase 2 where things are planned, but we don't really have a clue of the final baddie that's being led up to. Not many of those movies were really good back then either.  Another issue is with every new show and new movie, there's new strings attached to each project. Because every movie and show introduces new characters, they're all in different parts of space, and they're all building to new Infinity War-like movies. So they have to introduce new characters, introduce concepts like multiverses for audiences, and then sunset characters for actors who don't want to keep playing them or so they can take a break.   SPOILERS: So this movie had to introduce Gorr's daughter, sunset Natalie Portman's story, give Hemsworth a break, probably had to introduce the concept of the Gods, and push Tessa Thompson further. Not as much as some movies like Multiverse of Madness had to do, but they had goals of this movie they had to meet. So they can only play in that little box. Every single movie that comes out, the box to play in seems smaller and smaller.
